    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b1d7c502-69a8-4e5c-815e-f8ed17c193f0'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer5503033527021829749">Leo ha sedici anni: ama le chiacchiere con gli amici, il calcetto, le scorribande in motorino e vive in perfetta simbiosi con il suo iPod. Le ore di scuola sono uno strazio, i professori “una specie protetta che speri si estingua definitivamente”. <br/>Così, quando arriva un nuovo supplente di storia e filosofia, lui si prepara ad accoglierlo con cinismo e palline inzuppate di </span>
  <span id="freeText5503033527021829749" style="display:none">Leo ha sedici anni: ama le chiacchiere con gli amici, il calcetto, le scorribande in motorino e vive in perfetta simbiosi con il suo iPod. Le ore di scuola sono uno strazio, i professori “una specie protetta che speri si estingua definitivamente”. <br />Così, quando arriva un nuovo supplente di storia e filosofia, lui si prepara ad accoglierlo con cinismo e palline inzuppate di saliva. Ma questo giovane insegnante è diverso: una luce gli brilla negli occhi quando sprona gli studenti a cercare il proprio sogno. Leo ha un nemico che lo atterrisce: il bianco. <br />Il bianco è l’assenza, tutto ciò che ha a che fare con la privazione e la perdita è bianco. <br />Il rosso invece è il colore dell’amore, della passione, del sangue; rosso è il colore dei capelli di Beatrice. Perché un sogno Leo ce l’ha e si chiama Beatrice, anche se lei ancora non lo sa. Leo ha anche una realtà, Silvia, una presenza affidabile e serena. <br />Quando scopre che Beatrice è ammalata e che la malattia ha qualcosa a che fare con quel bianco che tanto lo spaventa, Leo dovrà scavare a fondo dentro di sé, sanguinare e rinascere, per capire che i sogni non possono morire e trovare il coraggio di credere in qualcosa di più grande.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5503033527021829749" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13396657393459636652">Favorite Quotes: <br/><br/>Perhaps she was a dog in her previous life? I enjoy giving people a former life in my head. It helps explain their character.<br/><br/>I can’t believe it. I am sleeping under the same roof as Beatrice and I didn’t even know it. This sends me into hyperkinetic rapture. <br/><br/>Mom yells at me to get out of the bathroom and stop doing indecent things. Why don’t grown-ups understand anything? What do they know about what’s going on in your head? They’re convinced that the only things in your head ar</span>
  <span id="freeText13396657393459636652" style="display:none">Favorite Quotes: <br /><br />Perhaps she was a dog in her previous life? I enjoy giving people a former life in my head. It helps explain their character.<br /><br />I can’t believe it. I am sleeping under the same roof as Beatrice and I didn’t even know it. This sends me into hyperkinetic rapture. <br /><br />Mom yells at me to get out of the bathroom and stop doing indecent things. Why don’t grown-ups understand anything? What do they know about what’s going on in your head? They’re convinced that the only things in your head are the ones they can’t do anymore. <br /><br />Teachers are like boa constrictors. They wrap themselves around you when you’re distracted, then wait until you breathe out to tighten their grasp.<br /><br />The worst thing about life is that there’s no instruction manual. With a cell phone you follow the instructions, and if it doesn’t work, there’s the warranty. You take it back and they give you a new one. Not so with life. If it doesn’t work, they don’t give you a new one. You’re stuck with the one you have—used, dirty, and malfunctioning.<br /><br />My Review: <br /><br />I wasn’t sure I was going to enjoy this book as I tend to avoid YA and it took a few beats to acclimate to the author’s innovative and slyly colorful writing style. I soon found myself fully immersed in the cleverly crafted and jagged, yet fascinatingly compelling, stream of consciousness of Leo, a post-pubescent teenaged boy whose thoughts tended to ramble and flit about in a captivating and heart-squeezing manner. Leo’s inner dialogue was wryly amusing as were his personal observations and hard-won and ironic teenaged wisdoms. <br /><br />This wily author well remembers the insecurities and dramatics of youth and demonstrated remarkable insight into the rapid variability of their intense and extreme emotions, which soar to exhilaration as quickly as they can plummet to the vast pit of despair. I reveled in Leo’s inner musings as he obsessed over every nuance of his infatuation with the lovely and angelic redheaded schoolgirl named Beatrice. His fertile imagination, creative use of nicknames, and fixation on defining colors kept a smirk on my face while reading. Leo’s world revolved around playing soccer, his batscooter, his study friend Silva, the drudgery of school and teachers, and his undeclared love for the perfection known as Beatrice. This ingeniously well-crafted story detailed Leo’s most transformative year of enlightening life-lessons.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13396657393459636652" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12772815645368449256">A fine way to advertise your book is to call it the Italian <i>'The Fault in our Stars'</i> which I admit was a YA book worth reading. But throw in a protagonist in the form of an irritating high schooler with the maturity of a 5 year old, that ugly cover and an extremely horrendous English translation and what you get is the exact opposite of the best-selling John Green book. <br/>Avoid.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50950278-iulia?shelf=honorable-mentions">honorable-mentions</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50950278-iulia?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50950278-iulia?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2438982329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15691108314724645326">I received a complimentary copy of this book from Thomas Nelson through NetGalley. Opinions expressed in this review are completely my own.<br/><br/>I had the chance to read an excerpt from this in Netgalley's Buzz Books, and I instantly knew that it would be a book that I would love. <br/><br/>I don't believe that the <i> Italian "Fault in Our Stars" </i> is an accurate description of what <i> White as Silence, Red as Song </i> really is. It honestly reminded me more of <i> Catcher in the Rye</i> or <i> The Perks of Being a Wallflower. </i><br/><br/>L</span>
  <span id="freeText15691108314724645326" style="display:none">I received a complimentary copy of this book from Thomas Nelson through NetGalley. Opinions expressed in this review are completely my own.<br /><br />I had the chance to read an excerpt from this in Netgalley's Buzz Books, and I instantly knew that it would be a book that I would love. <br /><br />I don't believe that the <i> Italian "Fault in Our Stars" </i> is an accurate description of what <i> White as Silence, Red as Song </i> really is. It honestly reminded me more of <i> Catcher in the Rye</i> or <i> The Perks of Being a Wallflower. </i><br /><br />Leo, the narrator, is a teenage boy trying to make sense of the world and suffering from all the typical teenage issues which often plague this sort of protagonist: the tediousness of school, furor of first love and desire to prove oneself to one's peers. Leo is a confident and genuine person, and I grew very fond of him as I read through the book. I enjoyed how the colors in the title are related to the quirky way in which Leo views the world, trying to attribute colors to people and feelings. I saw this as a way of simplifying the unknown, trying to rationalize an increasingly confusing world from the perspective of a sixteen year old.<br /><br />In his day to day life, Leo is a regular teen; he hates school, thinks teachers are lame, plays soccer and gets into trouble with his friends. He is fiercely enamored with Beatrice, a beautiful red-haired girl, even though he does not know her personally. While this may cause some readers to roll their eyes, the beauty and authenticity of Leo's feelings is undeniable in my opinion. <br /><br />The book is focused on the way Leo reacts when he discovers that Beatrice is suffering from leukemia, and follows the transformation on his initial infatuation into a different, more profound feeling. Two other relationships that are explored are Silvia, Leo's best friend and "guardian angel" and The Dreamer, a substitute teacher who, against all odds, befriends Leo and offers an adult perspective over the difficult situation.<br /><br />I loved this book because it was sad, beautiful and pure. I enjoyed the writing style and the first-person narration, it gave the story a personal touch and made me connect to the protagonists's worldview and feelings. I would warmly recommend this book to anyone who does not mind wading through a bit of teenage angst to get to a beautiful, touching story.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1330931897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1330931897" />
    <a title="mollusskka" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37421969-mollusskka"><img alt="mollusskka" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593311853p2/37421969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1330931897?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mollusskka" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mollusskka" href="/user/show/37421969-mollusskka">mollusskka</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9786022498179" href="/book/show/25220077-white-as-milk-red-as-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37421969-mollusskka?shelf=romance-garing">romance-garing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37421969-mollusskka?shelf=difilmkan">difilmkan</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1330931897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8056563234120497211">Like it or not, some part of this book did remind me of A Walk to Remember, The Catcher in the Rye, and The Perks of Being a Wallflower. The romance, the personality and the mind of the main character, and the relationship between the main character, Leo, with his teacher, sounds like Charlie and Bill to me. <br/><br/>It's a story of Leo, a coming of age boy who fell in love with a girl suffers from Leukemia, Beatrice. When other boys setting a goal to become a dentist, a painter or something else in the </span>
  <span id="freeText8056563234120497211" style="display:none">Like it or not, some part of this book did remind me of A Walk to Remember, The Catcher in the Rye, and The Perks of Being a Wallflower. The romance, the personality and the mind of the main character, and the relationship between the main character, Leo, with his teacher, sounds like Charlie and Bill to me. <br /><br />It's a story of Leo, a coming of age boy who fell in love with a girl suffers from Leukemia, Beatrice. When other boys setting a goal to become a dentist, a painter or something else in the future, Leo made Beatrice as his main goal/dream of his life, making him oblivious to the love his very best friend, Silvia, has for him. <br /><br />Unlike The Catcher in Rye, which I really loved, the story telling of this book was a so-so for me. But I like what Leo thinks about his surroundings. He's so genuine and can be so cynical sometimes, just like Holden. The romance between the three characters wasn't well-built, so I didn't shed a tear, which I think I should have. So, I guess the main story of this book is not about the romance. It's mainly about finding one's true self through reaching one's goal/dream. Maybe. <br /><br /><b>(For Sale: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/goodybook99/">https://www.instagram.com/goodybook99/</a> or <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.tokopedia.com/goodybook">https://www.tokopedia.com/goodybook</a>)</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8056563234120497211" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_113053892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/113053892" />
    <a title="The Anxious Bookaholic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic"><img alt="The Anxious Bookaholic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1290254839p2/3184360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/113053892?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Anxious Bookaholic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Anxious Bookaholic" href="/user/show/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic">The Anxious Bookaholic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9788425344244" href="/book/show/8051270-blanca-como-la-nieve-roja-como-la-sangre">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone ;]</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic?shelf=fave-ya">fave-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic?shelf=the-cutest-thing-ever">the-cutest-thing-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic?shelf=own-on-paper">own-on-paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3184360-the-anxious-bookaholic?shelf=first-time-i-read-this-author">first-time-i-read-this-author</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer113053892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6925284304129773143"> <b>I was born on the first day of school; I grew up and grew old only for two thousand days.</b><br/><br/> <br/> I feel like I’ve been waiting to read this book since forever and when I finally got my hands on it yesterday I just couldn’t stop. I probably should not write this review, since I closed the last page, just a few moments ago but I guess its stronger then me. <br/> I admit that the first thing that drew me to this book was the front cover –not just the fact that the girl is totally gorgeous; but the sadness in</span>
  <span id="freeText6925284304129773143" style="display:none"> <b>I was born on the first day of school; I grew up and grew old only for two thousand days.</b><br /><br /> <br /> I feel like I’ve been waiting to read this book since forever and when I finally got my hands on it yesterday I just couldn’t stop. I probably should not write this review, since I closed the last page, just a few moments ago but I guess its stronger then me. <br /> I admit that the first thing that drew me to this book was the front cover –not just the fact that the girl is totally gorgeous; but the sadness in her eyes, the fragile look on face that’s what really caught my eye. <br /> In White as milk, Red as blood we meet Leo, knocking on the front door of adulthood, he is in love with his motorbike without breaks, with his guitar, with football. But most of all he is in love with Beatrice – with her green eyes and red hair, she is the one that saves him from the white. She is his dream, his future, his everything. They are meant to be. She just doesn’t know that yet. It seems that nothing can come in the way of his romance, but then reality comes crashing in. Beatrice is sick, so Leo has to prove his love, in the small period of time that fate gives him, he has to grow up, grieve, reborn from the ashes and realize that dreams never die.<br /> White as milk, Red as blood is a brilliant book. I loved the plot, the characters. I even loved Terminator – Leo’s dog with problematic bladder. I loved the way one teacher managed to make him see through the problems and cheered for him to chase his dream. I loved the way it wasn’t just a typical high school novel. I loved the way this book educates you on so many different levels and leaves you still wanting for more.<br />Most of all I loved the way this book is like a giant palette of colors and all of them symbolize something important for Leo. White - the fear, the unknown, the absence, the lost; Blue – the sky, the sea, the harmony you feel when coming home, Silvia’s eyes; Red – the passion, blood, love, Beatrice’s hair, etc. <br /> The only thing that I am sorry about is that I can’t read the book in its original edition, in Italian.<br /> I recommend this book to everyone, who has the opportunity to read it since the book is new and it’s probably not translated in English yet. For those who already read it I hope you enjoyed it as much I did. Five stars for this amazing debut novel.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6925284304129773143" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2503485257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2503485257" />
    <a title="Maddy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40658811-maddy"><img alt="Maddy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575666185p2/40658811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2503485257?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maddy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maddy" href="/user/show/40658811-maddy">Maddy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40658811-maddy?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40658811-maddy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2503485257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2097172171676841321">To be perfectly honestly, I think that this book is either going to be a hit or miss. For me, it was a hit. <br/><br/>Leo, the main character, is a 16-year-old trying to make his way through life. He's tired of the white in his life, the plain and everyday routine. Beatrice is the girl with red hair. Red, the color of passion and love. The girl with the disease. <br/><br/>This book is honestly unlike any other book I've ever read. It's so deep and real, and I just loved it. The story is in first person and there is</span>
  <span id="freeText2097172171676841321" style="display:none">To be perfectly honestly, I think that this book is either going to be a hit or miss. For me, it was a hit. <br /><br />Leo, the main character, is a 16-year-old trying to make his way through life. He's tired of the white in his life, the plain and everyday routine. Beatrice is the girl with red hair. Red, the color of passion and love. The girl with the disease. <br /><br />This book is honestly unlike any other book I've ever read. It's so deep and real, and I just loved it. The story is in first person and there isn't a large amount of communication in it. A lot of the book is just Leo and his thoughts. At first I was a little unsure about how I liked it, but it definitely grew on me as the story went on. There definitely was some conversations between the characters, just not the normal amount you'd normally see in a book. <br /><br />I think what really sold me on this book though was when Leo's new teacher came into the picture. <br /><br />The Dreamer.<br /><br />He helped Leo get rid of the white in his life and he taught his class to not just take the easiest path. He taught them to dream. <br /><br />To wrap everything up, this is a beautiful yet deep book on passion and dreams. I am a huge dreamer and I absolutely loved every bit of it. As I said in the beginning of my review, I can definitely see people not liking it. It's different from your normal book, and I think that's what made me like it so much. There's heartache and pain, but there's also passion and love. <br /><br />"I received a free copy of this book from Thomas Nelson in exchange of my honest review. All thoughts are my own and I wasn't required to write a positive review."</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2528584185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2528584185" />
    <a title="Robyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6209444-robyn"><img alt="Robyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542943428p2/6209444.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2528584185?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robyn" href="/user/show/6209444-robyn">Robyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2528584185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12530468709328127456">Leo is your average high school student. He is only sixteen years old and acts like any normal teenager. He is in high school, but doesn't really like any of his classes or teachers. He has good friends, plays sports, and he is just living in the moment. He experiences his first crush in Beatrice, a girl a year ahead of him in school. She doesn't really know Leo other than in passing, but he loves her regardless. <br/><br/>Leo is infatuated with colors and hates white as it is the color of silence. White </span>
  <span id="freeText12530468709328127456" style="display:none">Leo is your average high school student. He is only sixteen years old and acts like any normal teenager. He is in high school, but doesn't really like any of his classes or teachers. He has good friends, plays sports, and he is just living in the moment. He experiences his first crush in Beatrice, a girl a year ahead of him in school. She doesn't really know Leo other than in passing, but he loves her regardless. <br /><br />Leo is infatuated with colors and hates white as it is the color of silence. White is nothing and Leo does not want to be white. He does not want to be alone, doesn’t know how to be alone and wants to feel as if he exists. Leo has a passion for red. Red is love. Red is what is tangible. Beatrice is red and Leo will do anything he can to make Beatrice see him, but when Beatrice gets sick will it be too late for Leo to tell Beatrice how he feels?<br /><br />Leo is not always an easy character to like in the beginning. Sure, he is a good person, but I felt he was lost in his own little world when it came to Beatrice. Everything was about his love for Beatrice and in turn he never actually saw what was right in front of his eyes. His good friend Sylvia. I don’t think Leo really took Sylvia’s thoughts into consideration and at times Leo felt very selfish. My feelings for Leo changed pretty quickly, though once Leo met The Dreamer, a substitute teacher who comes in to teach a Philosophy class. Leo finally starts to shine and become a likable protagonist for me. <br /><br />Leo finally learns what it means to dream and to have a passion for something. Leo puts his whole heart and soul into his dream and this is when he finally comes into his own and grows from his experience. It was amazing to watch him flourish and become an honorable and thoughtful teenager willing to help others, especially Beatrice. I could see how Leo wanted to make a difference and in doing so, he learned a lot about himself in the process.<br /><br />White as Silence, Red as Song has been compared to books such as A Fault in our Stars and while I can see a lot of similarities, I can also see this story being compared to A Walk to Remember especially with the beautiful passages and the deeper meaning behind certain things. It really is a highly emotional book, but not only is it emotional, it also makes you think about your own dreams. It really makes you think about what you want out of life. For myself, I did stop to think about my dreams and how I have pushed them to the side and this story makes me realize that without dreams what is your purpose in life?<br /><br />White as Silence, Red as Song is a beautifully moving and emotional coming of age story full of life lessons that we should all listen to. It is a story that will encourage you to think and to dream.. I highly recommend this book to anyone who likes an in depth story on par with the two books mentioned above. This story has found a place in my heart and renewed my faith in my own dreams I had previously pushed to the side.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12530468709328127456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2569410741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="OutlawPoet" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/245365-outlawpoet"><img alt="OutlawPoet" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600195942p2/245365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2569410741?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="OutlawPoet" class="user" itemprop="url" name="OutlawPoet" href="/user/show/245365-outlawpoet">OutlawPoet</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2569410741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9216703211725769921">This book sold about a million copies in Italy and was also made into a movie. It's hailed as an International entree into the 'Dying Teen' subgenre.<br/><br/>But it's really not.<br/><br/>This is a coming of age novel. Is there a dying teen? Yes. But it's not really about her or about their romance. It's about a teen named Leo who finally grows up.<br/><br/>Part of the difficulty for me may be cultural. I love Italy and Italian lit. However, when I read a YA book, I expect some authenticity. And while Leo felt like a self-c</span>
  <span id="freeText9216703211725769921" style="display:none">This book sold about a million copies in Italy and was also made into a movie. It's hailed as an International entree into the 'Dying Teen' subgenre.<br /><br />But it's really not.<br /><br />This is a coming of age novel. Is there a dying teen? Yes. But it's not really about her or about their romance. It's about a teen named Leo who finally grows up.<br /><br />Part of the difficulty for me may be cultural. I love Italy and Italian lit. However, when I read a YA book, I expect some authenticity. And while Leo felt like a self-centered teen boy, he never spoke authentically. None of our teen characters did.<br /><br />Instead, they spoke as if they were tenured professors of philosophy and poetry. Every sentence a metaphor on life and love and very existence. I ached for one of them - just one - to actually sound like a teenager.<br /><br />The book has some sadness, but it's tempered by the fact that we never really get to know our sick girl. Though we finally meet her, she speaks like Mother Theresa or some other suffering Saint and never feels like a real girl. She's dying and while it's nice that she can philosophize about colors and life and meaning, she's a teen. What about sex and love or even her first kiss? What about all the things she'll never get to experience?<br /><br />While I enjoyed the book overall and appreciated the poetic language, I was left unsatisfied. I wish this Dying Teen/Coming of Age Book had one character who actually felt like a real teenager.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2524232500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2524232500" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17864994-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519015688p2/17864994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2524232500?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/17864994-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17864994-rachel?shelf=netgalley-2018">netgalley-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17864994-rachel?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2524232500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer773741971351892412"><b>
  <i>A teen-aged boy’s self-discovery amidst illness and death is the focus of this translated coming-of-age novel by Alessandro D’Avenia.</i>
</b><br/><br/>I cannot tell you how eager I was for this book. It was dubbed as The Fault of Our Stars of Italy, and that alone got my attention. Add to that a very enticing blurb, and it won me over, so I requested it.<br/><br/>Sadly, <b>White as Silence, Red as Song</b> didn’t quite measure up to its potential.<br/><br/>The story follows and is told by 16-year old Leo. He’s witty and sarcastic: a ty</span>
  <span id="freeText773741971351892412" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>A teen-aged boy’s self-discovery amidst illness and death is the focus of this translated coming-of-age novel by Alessandro D’Avenia.</i>
</b><br /><br />I cannot tell you how eager I was for this book. It was dubbed as The Fault of Our Stars of Italy, and that alone got my attention. Add to that a very enticing blurb, and it won me over, so I requested it.<br /><br />Sadly, <b>White as Silence, Red as Song</b> didn’t quite measure up to its potential.<br /><br />The story follows and is told by 16-year old Leo. He’s witty and sarcastic: a typical teen-aged boy who, by all means, does typical teen-aged boy stuff – school, soccer, dare contests with his friend Niko, music. Reading from his perspective was a quart amusing, and annoying and just plain tiring for the rest of the way. Leo is really immature though he pretends to be all-knowing. He throws around these big words like “love” a lot when he doesn’t even understand what they mean. Given, he does grow a bit by the end of the book, but not by much.<br /><br />Another thing that bothered me was Leo’s obsession with Beatrice. He claims to be in love with her, but the most interaction the two has shared were just smiles as they pass each other in school hallways. He talks about her all the time, and not to discount how strong his feelings were, but Leo’s obsession with Beatrice was strange bordering on creepy. There was this one scene that really made me stop reading for a while. Leo, who was also confined at the same hospital as Beatrice after a scooter accident, goes to visit the girl. He just stayed in Beatrice’s room even if the girl was sleeping, and, more, he caresses her face, then proceeds to tell the nurse who sees him in the girl’s room that he is Beatrice’s boyfriend.<br /><br />I’m not sure if, somewhere along the way, things were lost in translation but the writing felt patchy and disjointed. It actually made this short book seem longer. I almost put it down a number of times.<br /><br />I just have to make it clear that I haven’t read the original, which was in Italian, so my review only applies to the English translation. I really wanted to like this book. It had potential, but that’s just it, potential.<br /><br /><i>eARC provided by the publisher via NetGalley for an honest review. This review was first published on <a href="https://inbetweenbookpages.wordpress.com/2018/09/18/review-white-as-silence-red-as-song-by-alessandro-davenia/" rel="nofollow noopener"><b>In Between Book Pages</b></a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="773741971351892412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2501172708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2501172708" />
    <a title="Kelly Gunderman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37983198-kelly-gunderman"><img alt="Kelly Gunderman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550376948p2/37983198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2501172708?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Gunderman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Gunderman" href="/user/show/37983198-kelly-gunderman">Kelly Gunderman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780785217060" href="/book/show/36576122-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2501172708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14104186981920258877">Check out this, other reviews, and more bookish things on my young adult book blog, <a href='http://www.herestohappyendings.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>Here's to Happy Endings!</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>***Actual Rating: 3.5/5 Stars***</i>
</b><br/><br/>I had a really difficult time trying to figure out whether or not this book was for me, and even still, while I'm torn about it, I do have to say that <em>White as Silence, Red as Song</em> is definitely a beautifully written book that prompts the reader to really think about what it is that they are taking in.<br/><br/><strong>I like books that make me think.</strong> I like books that tr</span>
  <span id="freeText14104186981920258877" style="display:none">Check out this, other reviews, and more bookish things on my young adult book blog, <a href="http://www.herestohappyendings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Here's to Happy Endings!</a><br /><br /><b>
  <i>***Actual Rating: 3.5/5 Stars***</i>
</b><br /><br />I had a really difficult time trying to figure out whether or not this book was for me, and even still, while I'm torn about it, I do have to say that <em>White as Silence, Red as Song</em> is definitely a beautifully written book that prompts the reader to really think about what it is that they are taking in.<br /><br /><strong>I like books that make me think.</strong> I like books that truly make me appreciate life, that make me look at the simple things around me and go "Wow, I'm so glad I have this." Even more do I love the books that give me a good appreciation for the <em>people</em> in my life - my husband, my daughters, my parents - all of them. <em>White as Silence, Red as Song</em> made me thankful that I have my family.<br /><br />This book has been compared to <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>. Let me say first off that I haven't read <em>The Fault in Our Stars</em>, as I tend to try to avoid super hyped up books (because I always end up being the black sheep and not enjoying it as much as everyone led me to believe I would). Therefore, I really can't compare the two, but I did think that this book had a lot of emotional parts that will leave the reader with a lot of emotions to sort through. But while I thought that it came through for the most part, with that comparison alone I kind of expected to feel a bit more? Still, it was a really good novel.<br /><br /><strong><em>White as Silence, Red as</em> <em>Song</em> is a book that I read through in one day, from start to finish, without putting it down.</strong> It's rare that I have the ability (or the motivation) to do that with a novel, but this was on the shorter side and I kind of just pushed everything else off my plate and sat down to enjoy it.<br /><p>
  
    <em>
      <strong>"Everything is a color. Every emotion is a color."</strong>
    </em>
  
</p><br />Sixteen year old Leo loves hanging out with his friends, playing soccer with them, and writing - he writes often. While he doesn't care much for school, that all changes when a new teacher shows up and challenges the way he thinks. At first, Leo figures he will be like all the other teachers - no one of interest that would do anything influential for his life. Only Leo turns out to be wrong, because this new teacher is about to change a lot about his life.<br /><p>
  
    <em>
      <strong>"Beatrice is red. The easy love is red. A tempest. A hurricane that sweeps you away. An earthquake that crumbles your body to pieces. That's how I feel every time I see her. She doesn't know it yet, but one of these days I'll tell her."</strong>
    </em>
  
</p><br /><strong>Leo has a crush on a girl named Beatrice.</strong> Beatrice doesn't pay much attention to Leo, and the two almost never talk. Until one day, Beatrice isn't in school, and Leo finds out that she has been diagnosed with leukemia. When she comes back to school, Leo is still in love with her, and wants to tell her about it, but doesn't get the chance to, as he is taken to the hospital due to an accident shortly after. However, Leo finds out that Beatrice is also in the hospital, and she isn't doing very well - her cancer has come back. Leo uses this opportunity to get a closer look at Beatrice. He even gets up the nerve to write her a note telling her how he feels, but when he goes to deliver it to her, Beatrice is no longer in the hospital.<br /><p>
  
    <em>
      <strong>"'A life without dreams is like a garden without flowers, but a life full of impossible dreams is like a garden full of fake flowers...'"</strong>
    </em>
  
</p><br />When Leo starts going to Beatrice's house to see her, spending time with her, he finally gets to know the girl that he has been in love with for years. However, their time together is limited, and Leo must come to terms with the fact that Beatrice will not be around forever.<br /><br /><strong><em>White as Silence, Red as Song</em> is definitely an emotional read, and even thinking back on it now, there is so much happening in Leo's life, so much he has to learn about and come to terms with, while still being a teenage boy.</strong> I really enjoyed how the story was written from Leo's point of view, and I thought it was great to have a really clear look into his mind - what he was thinking, what he was writing, what was really making him feel the way he felt.<br /><br /><strong>I did feel that Leo was a bit stalker-ish through the book at times, and he acted a bit questionably on a few occasions, but nothing bad, honestly. </strong>Just a tad...strange? His character was interesting - definitely not your cookie cutter type - he really had thoughts and emotions that I don't think I would have seen coming, and I liked how he grew as a person through the book. I'm a huge fan of character growth, so that was a huge plus for me.<br /><br /><em>White as Silence, Red as Song</em> is one of those books that has beautiful writing and a great story behind it, and I have to give the book a lot of praise for that. I thought it was a pretty good read, and I would definitely recommend it to someone who wants something emotional and well thought out that has a lot of substance to it.<br /><br /><b>Note:</b> I received a copy of this book from the publisher in exchange for an honest review. Thank you!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14104186981920258877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2513186810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2513186810" />
    <a title="Vicky Again" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57349823-vicky-again"><img alt="Vicky Again" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585788568p2/57349823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2513186810?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vicky Again" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vicky Again" href="/user/show/57349823-vicky-again">Vicky Again</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2513186810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11909335262367554190">This book has <b>so much potential</b>, and I really hope that the version I read goes through a few more touch ups before it's published. <br/><br/>Because seriously--an Italian TFIOS! a coming of age story! These are all really great elements. <br/><br/>Yet, this book ended up being a let down for me for multiple reasons. <br/><br/>My biggest issue with this book is honestly the narrator. I just really <strong>did not like Leo</strong> for most of the novel. He consistently <strong>hates on teachers</strong> and calls them losers for no reason, he <strong>blames everyone</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText11909335262367554190" style="display:none">This book has <b>so much potential</b>, and I really hope that the version I read goes through a few more touch ups before it's published. <br /><br />Because seriously--an Italian TFIOS! a coming of age story! These are all really great elements. <br /><br />Yet, this book ended up being a let down for me for multiple reasons. <br /><br />My biggest issue with this book is honestly the narrator. I just really <strong>did not like Leo</strong> for most of the novel. He consistently <strong>hates on teachers</strong> and calls them losers for no reason, he <strong>blames everyone but himself</strong> (i.e. blaming his parents for faulty DNA), is self absorbed most of the time, is embarrased to talk to his mom, and <strong>cares about very little</strong>.<br /><br />Maybe Italian teens are different from American teens (seriously, why would you disrespect a teacher?), or <strong>D'Avenia just doesn't understand teenagers</strong> (I'm leaning towards the latter).<br /><br />It was just almost ridiculous how immature Leo was, and I was really not into him. <br /><br />Part of this might have been because of the translation. Although I <b>liked the writing style</b> and thought it was concise and less flowerly (compared to John Green), Leo's voice just really grated on me (that doesn't mean it will with you, but for me, he was almost infuriating at times). <br /><br />Yet, I still liked the writing style and I still liked the short-ish chapters and I liked all the personal thought. I just...didn't like Leo himself.<br /><br />But really, some of the translation was honestly kind of weird. Like, they use "you queer!" as an insult and I'm just ??? <br /><br />So there were definitely areas that were a bit funky with translation (i.e. I'm pretty sure the direct translation of the Italian title is "White as Milk, Red as Blood" but they changed it to make it sound better). I'm crossing my fingers that this is fixed in the final. <br /><br />And <b>the love triangle wasn't terrible, but it also wasn't great</b>. (Which I also blame on Leo.) I actually really enjoyed the Silvia x Leo dynamic, although I do think he didn't deserve her, but Leo incessantly pining over Beatrice, a girl he has barely ever spoken to and literally just likes on account of her hair, felt ridiculous and sort of out there. <br /><br />I feel like this is a book younger YA readers will enjoy and readers looking for a book similar to <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>, but obviously not as good. It's like the <i>Divergent</i> to a <i>The Hunger Games</i>. It has a lot of potential, but I feel like the execution--whether it's from the author's actual writing or the translation--combined with a protagonist I didn't really like made this to be not a very enjoyable read for me. <br /><br /><i>Thank you so much to Netgalley, Thomas Nelson Books, and the Fantastic Flying Book Club for providing me with a digital review copy in exchange for an honest review!</i></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2662911533" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2662911533" />
    <a title="Rebekah Gyger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8314848-rebekah-gyger"><img alt="Rebekah Gyger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562021193p2/8314848.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2662911533?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah Gyger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah Gyger" href="/user/show/8314848-rebekah-gyger">Rebekah Gyger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780785217060" href="/book/show/36576122-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2662911533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3432470868764166857">I am always up for a novel that has been translated into English, both because it helps support the arts from other cultures and because it allows a glimpse into life outside of the English speaking worldview.<br/><br/>This book is told solely from the perspective of Leo, a teenage boy who starts of the book behaving like all the children who made me give up substitute teaching. And for that reason, I definitely had a hard time getting into the beginning of the story. However, as the story progressed and </span>
  <span id="freeText3432470868764166857" style="display:none">I am always up for a novel that has been translated into English, both because it helps support the arts from other cultures and because it allows a glimpse into life outside of the English speaking worldview.<br /><br />This book is told solely from the perspective of Leo, a teenage boy who starts of the book behaving like all the children who made me give up substitute teaching. And for that reason, I definitely had a hard time getting into the beginning of the story. However, as the story progressed and life started to challenge Leo's perceptions, the personality he had began to change, and this Leo I liked much better.<br /><br />The narrative of the novel is a poetic one, with most of the story told in introspective metaphors. And this introspection was what drew me to the later part of the story, despite the fact that I usually do not care for poetic narratives. However, while being beautiful analogies, many of the metaphors rely on sound or look alike words. And since this book was translated from Italian, those words no longer look or sound the same. Unfortunately, there was likely a lot that was lost in the translation simply because of the way the author used language to tell his story the first time and not by fault of the translator.<br /><br />In the end, this book may take some getting used to. The reader needs to be alright with a poetic narrative which does not hold up as well in English. As well as overlook how well the adults in the story recognize Leo's teenage angst for what it is-- a cry for help as he struggles to understand a world that is no longer as simple and colorful as he thought it was, and how easily he accepts their attempts to help him.<br /><br />I did enjoyed it by the end and would be interested in reading other translated works of D'Avenia's, should any of those be made.<br /><br />I have provided an honest review after having received a copy of the book through the Fiction Guild. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3432470868764166857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18879322-white-like-milk-red-like-blood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5892196-carole-carole-s-random-life-in-books?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer14593361389057466594">In the interest of full disclosure, I received an advance reader edition of this book from Open Road Integrated Media and Net Galley for the purpose of review.<br/><br/>This is Leo's story. It is a story of love, loss, connections, separations, death, grief, life, fear, friendship, learning, and growth. Leo brings the reader along during this pivotal point in his life.<br/><br/>Leo falls in love with Beatrice despite the fact that they have never spoken. He is an average teen who plays on the soccer team with his f</span>
  <span id="freeText14593361389057466594" style="display:none">In the interest of full disclosure, I received an advance reader edition of this book from Open Road Integrated Media and Net Galley for the purpose of review.<br /><br />This is Leo's story. It is a story of love, loss, connections, separations, death, grief, life, fear, friendship, learning, and growth. Leo brings the reader along during this pivotal point in his life.<br /><br />Leo falls in love with Beatrice despite the fact that they have never spoken. He is an average teen who plays on the soccer team with his friend Niko and hangs out and studies with his friend Silvia. His class get a substitute at the beginning of the year who challenges Leo to think. Leo learns that Beatrice is sick with leukemia and decides to give her a letter. He is injured and the letter is never delivered. He does eventually spend time with Beatrice, who later dies after becoming his friend. <br /><br />During this journey, Leo connects with the substitute "the Dreamer" and his father in a way that has not happened before. He runs into a few conflict with his friend Niko when his priorities chance and soccer is not longer what is most important to him. He thinks of Silvia as only a friend and can not see what is right in front of him until the end of the book.<br /><br />This book started out difficult for me. It felt a bit choppy and I was not connecting with the characters. Then something clicked and the book flowed and I felt the pain and uncertainty in Leo's heart. I do recommend this book to anyone who enjoys a good coming of age story.</span>

<div id="review_2185375973" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2185375973" />
    <a title="Hallie Szott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6447247-hallie-szott"><img alt="Hallie Szott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541714070p2/6447247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2185375973?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hallie Szott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hallie Szott" href="/user/show/6447247-hallie-szott">Hallie Szott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780785217060" href="/book/show/36576122-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6447247-hallie-szott?shelf=books-for-review">books-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6447247-hallie-szott?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6447247-hallie-szott?shelf=beat-the-backlist-2019">beat-the-backlist-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6447247-hallie-szott?shelf=bookish-bingo-jan-2019">bookish-bingo-jan-2019</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6447247-hallie-szott?shelf=mount-tbr-2019">mount-tbr-2019</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2185375973" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6258887266443000853">3.5<br/><br/>White as Silence, Red as Song is an odd YA story. Leo carries it with a stream-of-consciousness-esque narration, so naturally, it focuses on the aspects of his life: school, soccer, friends, and his crush on Beatrice. At times, Leo comes across immature and makes questionable decisions (he is a teenage boy, after all), but his growth through the story, thanks to injury, illness, and a teacher that makes him think, is interesting to see.<br/><br/>When I picked up White as Silence, Red as Song, the compa</span>
  <span id="freeText6258887266443000853" style="display:none">3.5<br /><br />White as Silence, Red as Song is an odd YA story. Leo carries it with a stream-of-consciousness-esque narration, so naturally, it focuses on the aspects of his life: school, soccer, friends, and his crush on Beatrice. At times, Leo comes across immature and makes questionable decisions (he is a teenage boy, after all), but his growth through the story, thanks to injury, illness, and a teacher that makes him think, is interesting to see.<br /><br />When I picked up White as Silence, Red as Song, the comparison to The Fault in Our Stars helped me to have an idea of what type of story I was entering—and kept me from fully investing emotionally with the characters, I think. Even so, I found that Alessandro D’Avenia’s novel had enough differences to make it unique. It’s a quick, thought-provoking read that YA readers could enjoy.<br /><br />This review is also posted on <a href="https://pagebypagebookbybook.blogspot.com/2019/01/white-as-silence-red-as-song-book-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Hallie Reads</a>.<br /><br />Thanks to BookLook Bloggers, I received a complimentary copy of White as Silence, Red as Song and the opportunity to provide an honest review. I was not required to write a positive review, and all the opinions I have expressed are my own.<br /><br /><br />Reading Challenge Categories:<br />-Beat the Backlist Reading Bingo: From your 2018 TBR<br />-Hope By the Book Reading Challenge: Young adult genre<br />-January Bookish Bingo: A book you meant to read in 2018<br />-Modern Mrs. Darcy Reading Challenge: A book by an author who is new to you<br />-Popsugar Reading Challenge: A book you meant to read in 2018</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36178590-michelle?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2529132401" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17711642721048216131">This was a heart warming story of a young man in high school and how he falls in love with a girl who is diagnosed with Leukemia. I found it refreshing to read about young love and the many trials and tribulations that come along with being a typical teenager. I felt many emotions while reading this book. Some parts made me laugh, some parts made me happy, and some parts made me feel sad.<br/><br/>The main character Leo has quite a way with words and was easy to like as a character in the book. I enjoyed </span>
  <span id="freeText17711642721048216131" style="display:none">This was a heart warming story of a young man in high school and how he falls in love with a girl who is diagnosed with Leukemia. I found it refreshing to read about young love and the many trials and tribulations that come along with being a typical teenager. I felt many emotions while reading this book. Some parts made me laugh, some parts made me happy, and some parts made me feel sad.<br /><br />The main character Leo has quite a way with words and was easy to like as a character in the book. I enjoyed reading about his daily life, his thought process and the way he thinks. He has quite the imagination and is a typical teenager.<br /><br />It was interesting to see the world through his eyes and the way he interprets it in various colours. White is silent and boring. Leo doesn't want to be white or boring. Blue is the colour of friendship and this is how he sees all of his friends, including Silvia - one of his closest female friends. Red is the colour of love and this is the colour he sees when he looks at Beatrice, the woman he loves.<br /><br />This book was quite interesting and it makes you think deeply. It was a wonderful book to read and I enjoyed it from beginning to the very end. It is a story of setting hopes, goals and dreams and then working to attain those. White as Silence, Red as Song is a great story of love, friendship, heartache, and chasing your dreams in an attempt to make them come true.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2455123520" />
    <a title="Michaela Bush" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46112488-michaela-bush"><img alt="Michaela Bush" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520866736p2/46112488.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2455123520?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michaela Bush" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michaela Bush" href="/user/show/46112488-michaela-bush">Michaela Bush</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780785217077" href="/book/show/36911793-white-as-silence-red-as-song">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2455123520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13548027949602181961">I received a complimentary copy of this book from Thomas Nelson through NetGalley. Opinions expressed in this review are completely my own. <br/>This book seemed like it would be very interesting, and I am still struggling to decide how I felt about it...hence the rating. I found it as confusing as Dante's work itself, and I'm not sure if this was clever and purposeful or merely a writing choice that could have been changed. I considered putting it down several times, but once I was halfway through, </span>
  <span id="freeText13548027949602181961" style="display:none">I received a complimentary copy of this book from Thomas Nelson through NetGalley. Opinions expressed in this review are completely my own. <br />This book seemed like it would be very interesting, and I am still struggling to decide how I felt about it...hence the rating. I found it as confusing as Dante's work itself, and I'm not sure if this was clever and purposeful or merely a writing choice that could have been changed. I considered putting it down several times, but once I was halfway through, the book started to grip me. It has several interesting morals that I can appreciate, such as the struggle to live your dreams, to love, and to sacrifice everything. Something I was shocked by, however, was the presence of profanity (mild; PG-13) and the fact that the main character grappled with trying to decide between evolution, reincarnation, and the existence of God -- somewhat disappointing, coming from Thomas Nelson. I also felt as though I was reading about 13 year olds rather than 16 year olds, who should be somewhat more in control of their emotions, hormones, and --yes, know how to mail a letter! I have to say that I loved Silvia and The Dreamer, perhaps feeling more for them than I did the main character and Beatrice, who seemed painfully unattainable to the point that I almost wished he would give up and see reality. <br /><br />Overall, it was an interesting book but, as Dante's work, I'm torn between saying it was a jumble of side-stories or saying it was an artful story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13548027949602181961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText607371029093641851" style="display:none"><b>Sono nato il primo giorno di scuola, cresciuto e invecchiato in soli duecento giorni.</b><br /><br /><br />This book was amazing. Moving. Funny and touching at the same time.<br /><br />It left me speechless. The simple writing, perfect for the thoughts of a sixteen-year old boy, and the bare clarity of his feelings made this book a piece of art, a sublime example of an high school student in love whose life suddenly changes, and not in a good way.<br /><br /><br />The hero's name is Leo.<br />Beatrice is his life, his heart, his happiness, his <i>
  <b>red</b>
</i>.<br />And his love for her?<br /><i>
  <b>Love is blood-red.</b>
</i><br /><br />And fear is pure, unaltered white.<br /><br />And when he discovers that Beatrice's got <i>leukaemia</i>, that her blood is slowly turning white, he's afraid. But he's got Silvia. His best friend. And even though Silvia is not <b>
  <i>red</i>
</b>, she is peace.<br /><br /><br />When things get worse, Leo doesn't know what to do, what to think, how to go on; but Silvia, his father, Professor Dreamer, God and, why not, even Dante will help him through the sorrow.<br /><br /><br />And during these months, Leo has the opportunity of learning to truly give and receive love.<br />Because sometimes, what matters is not to get your happy ending, but what you manage to give before the end.<br /><br />And sometimes, you can learn to love again.</span>

  <span id="freeText8332146874263288547" style="display:none">I have never read or seen the movie for the Fault in our Stars. Therefore, I can not compare this book to it as some other readers have. Yet, I will tell you that this book didn't really deliver for me. The theme is "love makes everything possible". Thus the reason that Leo felt he could do anything including being Beatrice knight in shining armor. <br /><br />Here is why this book didn't really work for me. I felt a bit uncomfortable to the point that Leo came off as kind of stalkerish. He kept obsessing about Beatrice. Yet, he didn't have for a good portion of the story a "real" connection with her. Well not face to face when she was aware of Leo. He visited her in the hospital while she was sleeping. Additionally, the way the book was written kind of like a poem, made it kind of hard to stay grounded in the story. Plus, it moved really fast. This book was a good effort but it missed the mark. </span>

It shuttered it, and than threw it and broke more. It is put back together at the end, but the pieces don't fit the same anymore.... <br /><br />This story starts funny. And I laughed at teenage Leo. At his typical teenage behavior. ( Hey, we all have been there). <span id="freeTextContainer16219713653705693862">Sixteen-year-old Leo is in love. He is too shy to approach red-haired Beatrice, until he learns that she is ill with leukemia. He decides to do all he can to make her life better at this difficult time. But it is when he experiences terrible loss that he discovers what he has really wanted all along!<br/><br/>I love how this book is written. Leo narrates his story, and, as I read this book, it was as if an actual teenage boy was telling me his story. Leo is very real, thus making this story unforgettable.</span>
  <span id="freeText16219713653705693862" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Leo is in love. He is too shy to approach red-haired Beatrice, until he learns that she is ill with leukemia. He decides to do all he can to make her life better at this difficult time. But it is when he experiences terrible loss that he discovers what he has really wanted all along!<br /><br />I love how this book is written. Leo narrates his story, and, as I read this book, it was as if an actual teenage boy was telling me his story. Leo is very real, thus making this story unforgettable. It is about growing up. It is also about seeing what you already have. Beautifully and realistically written, this book is to be experienced!<br /><br />I was given a free copy of this book in exchange for an unbiased review.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText16690432959832485056" style="display:none">received a complimentary copy of this book from Thomas Nelson through NetGalley.   function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QXVl3oFWPSREtk54USVOCQekxyES/c8WKp8FmmZdFNB3N+JGcRM5gJYDn106xnZn2OIXYwGeDAeJTPXlFKHCjA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wOoQTELmWGBtiU45upOLOlLjREMUIQYhLocJ/GJai2f2qJfUsqNcxL88nxzRcLNUjaWUAQdCxTCNVPmDEKZdOw==')})
  }

Ci sono Carlo e Alice: stessa classe e, a volte, stesso banco. Lui è meravigl<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText4976306007538410305\" style=\"display:none\">C\'è una generazione fatta di sms, gavettoni, crèpes alla nutella, professori frustrati; c\'è la voglia di essere ascoltati e di giudicare la vita, gli adulti, l\'ingiustizia. Ci sono Carlo e Alice: stessa classe e, a volte, stesso banco. Lui è meravigliosamente imbranato, senza modelli da incarnare, senza maschere. Lei si sente diversa, non omologata, è uno spirito critico e, al contempo, una sognatrice. Il loro cuore è ancora poco addestrato, bravissimo a sbagliare. E così Alice casca tra le braccia di Giorgio, nascosto e intrigante. Carlo si lascia sedurre da Ludovica, la classica ragazza facile che sa il fatto suo. Diciotto anni. Due ragazzi si affacciano su un mondo adulto che capiscono poco, tanto più se la scuola, la famiglia e gli amici si mettono di mezzo... Ma le stelle quante sono è un romanzo senza peli sulla lingua, schietto, diretto, una freccia che va dritta al bersaglio. Una partita di ping-pong sentimentale. Con una bella ventata di romanticismo. Un libro a due facce. A due sessi. A due voci. È come se madre e figlia si scrutassero da lontano, o si spiassero, immobilizzate da una troppo severa autocoscienza. Bisogna tornare indietro. E Giulia lo fa. Torna a riflettere sulla giovinezza ferita dall\'egoismo e dalla prepotenza di una sorella falsamente perbenista, sul culto delle apparenze della madre e sul conforto che le viene da una giovane monaca peruviana, Sofia. Torna a rivivere i primi passi da medico, fra corsie e sale operatorie, il matrimonio con un primario, la lunga attesa di una maternità sofferta e desiderata. Più la storia di Giulia si snoda nel buio del passato, più affiorano misteri che chiedono di essere sciolti. E il legno si ammorbidisce. Ma per madre e figlia l\'incontro può solo avvenire a costo di pagare il prezzo di una verità difficile, fuori da ogni finzione.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"11548765955067696742\" href=\"#\" Immergendosi nella sofferenza e superandola, ci ricorda come sia sempre possibile buttarsi alle spalle la sfiducia per andare al di là dei nostri limiti. Massimo Gramellini ha raccolto gli slanci e le ferite di una vita priva del suo appiglio più solido. Una lotta incessante contro la solitudine, l\'inadeguatezza e il senso di abbandono, raccontata con passione e delicata ironia. Forse diventare grandi significa imparare ad amare e a perdonare, fare un lungo viaggio alla ricerca del tempo che abbiamo perso e che non abbiamo più.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5310935.Alessandro_D_Avenia">About Alessandro D&#39;Avenia</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/5310935.Alessandro_D_Avenia"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1366374306p3/5310935.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/5310935.Alessandro_D_Avenia">Alessandro D'Avenia
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
651
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17520921943357029891">Alessandro D’Avenia, born in 1977 in Palermo, holds a PhD in classics and is a high school literature teacher and screenwriter.<br/><br/>D'Avenia nasce il 2 maggio 1977 da Rita e Giuseppe D'Avenia, terzo di sei figli. Dal 1990 frequenta il liceo classico Vittorio Emanuele II di Palermo, dove incontra padre Pino Puglisi che insegnava religione nello stesso istituto e dalla cui figura viene fortemente influen</span>
  <span id="freeText17520921943357029891" style="display:none">Alessandro D’Avenia, born in 1977 in Palermo, holds a PhD in classics and is a high school literature teacher and screenwriter.<br /><br />D'Avenia nasce il 2 maggio 1977 da Rita e Giuseppe D'Avenia, terzo di sei figli. Dal 1990 frequenta il liceo classico Vittorio Emanuele II di Palermo, dove incontra padre Pino Puglisi che insegnava religione nello stesso istituto e dalla cui figura viene fortemente influenzato, così come da quella dell'insegnante di lettere.<br />Nel 1995 si trasferisce a Roma per frequentare all'Università La Sapienza la facoltà di lettere classiche. Nel 2000 si laurea in lettere classiche. Nel 2004 consegue il dottorato di ricerca in letteratura greca con specializzazione in Antropologia del mondo antico, terminandolo con una tesi sulle "sirene" in Omero e il loro rapporto con le Muse nel mondo antico. Mentre è impegnato col dottorato, insegna per tre anni nelle scuole medie. Finito il dottorato, preferisce l’insegnamento alla ricerca e frequenta la scuola di specializzazione per l’insegnamento secondario, al termine della quale insegna greco e latino al liceo. Fonda una compagnia teatrale dilettante e gira un cortometraggio.<br />La sua attività di scrittore inizia contemporaneamente a quella di insegnante. Il successo arriva per D'Avenia con il romanzo <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8737890._Bianca_come_il_latte__rossa_come_il_sangue" title=" Bianca come il latte, rossa come il sangue" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bianca come il latte, rossa come il sangue</a>, che diventa presto un best-seller e viene pubblicato in 20 paesi stranieri. Il successo del romanzo d'esordio viene parzialmente confermato dal secondo titolo di D'Avenia, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12999738._Cose_che_nessuno_sa" title=" Cose che nessuno sa" rel="nofollow noopener"> Cose che nessuno sa</a>.<br />Collabora come pubblicista con alcuni quotidiani italiani (Avvenire, La Stampa).<br />Come sceneggiatore, nel 2008 ha firmato alcuni episodi della terza serie di "Life Bites - Pillole di vita" presso Disney Italia. Nel 2011-2012 lavora alla sceneggiatura del film tratto da Bianca come il latte, rossa come il sangue, prodotto da Rai Cinema, che esce nelle sale cinematografiche nel mese di aprile 2013.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17520921943357029891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
